   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiceless velar stop
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">

         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiceless velar stop
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        voiceless velar plosive
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in many
       <a href="/wiki/Spoken_language" title="Spoken language">
        spoken languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents this sound is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        k
       </span>
       ⟩, and the equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        k
       </code>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [k]
       </span>
       sound is a very common sound cross-linguistically. Most languages have at least a plain
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [k]
       </span>
       , and some distinguish more than one variety. Most
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">
        Indo-Aryan languages
       </a>
       , such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">
        Hindi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">
        Bengali
       </a>
       , have a two-way contrast between
       <a href="/wiki/Aspirated_consonant" title="Aspirated consonant">
        aspirated
       </a>
       and plain
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [k]
       </span>
       . Only a few languages lack a voiceless velar stop, e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/Tahitian_language" title="Tahitian language">
        Tahitian
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Some languages have the
       <b>
        voiceless pre-velar stop
       </b>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which is articulated slightly more front compared with the place of articulation of the prototypical voiceless velar stop, though not as front as the prototypical
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_stop" title="Voiceless palatal stop">
        voiceless palatal stop
       </a>
       - see that article for more information.
      </p>
      <p>
       Conversely, some languages have the
       <b>
        voiceless post-velar stop
       </b>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which is articulated slightly behind the place of articulation of the prototypical voiceless velar stop, though not as back as the prototypical
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_stop" title="Voiceless uvular stop">
        voiceless uvular stop
       </a>
       - see that article for more information.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiceless_velar_stop&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiceless velar stop:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Occlusive" title="Occlusive">
         occlusive
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by obstructing airflow in the vocal tract. Since the consonant is also oral, with no
        <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">
         nasal outlet
        </a>
        , the airflow is blocked entirely, and the consonant is a
        <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
         stop
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">
         velar
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the back of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue" title="Tongue">
         tongue
        </a>
        (the dorsum) at the
        <a href="/wiki/Soft_palate" title="Soft palate">
         soft palate
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiceless, which means it is produced without vibrations of the vocal cords. In some languages the vocal cords are actively separated, so it is always voiceless; in others the cords are lax, so that it may take on the voicing of adjacent sounds.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

                       <p>
                        Where symbols appear in pairs, the leftmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" title="Voiceless consonant">
                         voiceless consonant
                        </a>
                        , and the rightmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" title="Voiced consonant">
                         voiced consonant
                        </a>
                        .
